## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators and damping/forcing ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt with inputs (t, v) indicates learning a first-order dynamical law for velocity (acceleration) in an oscillator-like system. With no position variable available, the most plausible physical content is velocity-dependent restoring/damping effects and/or explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation typical in nonlinear vibration models.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant bias acceleration: dv_dt = c0 (constant external acceleration/offset force per unit mass)
- Linear viscous damping (free decay in velocity space): dv_dt = c0 * v (exponential growth/decay rate in v)
- Quadratic drag (high-Re damping): dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping proportional to v|v|)
- Cubic nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation or nonlinear actuator response)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction: dv_dt = c0 * Sign(v) (approximately constant-magnitude friction opposing motion, in acceleration units)
- Mixed viscous + Coulomb friction: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * Sign(v) (combined linear damping and dry friction)
- Power-law drag/friction: dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v)**c1 (generalized resistive force scaling with speed)
- Stribeck-like friction curve: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * Sign(v) * exp(c2 * Abs(v)) (velocity-weakening/strengthening friction via exponential-in-speed term)
- Rayleigh-type negative damping at small speeds: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (with c0 > 0, c1 < 0 gives self-excitation with nonlinear saturation)
- Van-der-Pol-like pumping term in v-only form: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v (negative damping for small |v| and positive for large |v|, produces limit-cycle-like regulation in v)
- Sinusoidal forcing (external drive): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v (periodic excitation plus damping/gain)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (driving with harmonics/subharmonics)
- Parametrically modulated damping/gain: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * v (time-varying damping typical of parametrically excited systems)
- Nonlinear forced damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (canonical structure for driven nonlinear velocity dynamics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Viscous dissipation → terms proportional to v (dv_dt ∝ -v gives exponential decay of velocity).
- High-speed fluid drag → terms proportional to v*Abs(v) or v*Abs(v)**c (nonlinear damping that dominates at large |v|).
- Dry friction effects → Sign(v) contributions (nearly constant opposing acceleration, non-smooth at v = 0).
- Self-excited oscillation surrogate in velocity space → (c - v**2)*v or v + v**3 with opposing signs (energy injection at small |v| and saturation at large |v|).
- Periodic external driving → sin(c*t + phase) added to dv_dt (imposes oscillations at driving frequency).
- Multiple time scales or harmonics in excitation → sums of sinusoids with different frequencies in t.
- Parametric excitation/modulation → coefficients of v depend periodically on t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*v (Mathieu-like mechanism expressed through damping/gain modulation).
- Velocity-weakening/strengthening friction → exponential dependence on Abs(v) multiplying Sign(v) or v (captures rapid change of friction with speed).
- Odd symmetry in velocity-dependent forces → using odd functions of v (v, v**3, v*Abs(v)**c) to respect reversal symmetry of drag/friction with direction.
- Coexistence of smooth and non-smooth dissipation → combining v (smooth) with Sign(v) (non-smooth) to fit stick-slip-like acceleration signatures.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO3)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
-0.9687939560\,v\;+\;0.1062569142\sin(t)\;-\;0.4843969780\sin(v)
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **simultaneously**:
1) a linear-in-\(v\) term,  
2) a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no amplitude depending on \(v\)),  
3) a pure \(\sin(v)\) term (no absolute values, no piecewise),  
and **no extra functional dependence** (no exp/log/Max leftovers).

Key obstacle: none of the candidates contain a plain \(\sin(v)\) term at all. Many contain \(\cos(t)\) (convertible to \(\sin(t)\) by phase shift), but the \(-0.4844\sin(v)\) part is missing structurally.

Now check each candidate:

1. \(c0 v + c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\cos t\). Can match linear \(v\) and \(\sin(t)\) via \(\cos\) phase shift; but **no \(\sin(v)\)**. Setting \(c1=0\) removes exp, still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

2. Adds \(c4 v\max(0,c5+|v|)\): introduces piecewise/|v| nonlinearity; can be zeroed with \(c4=0\), but still reduces to (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

3. Adds \(\max(0,c5+|v|)\) term; can set \(c4=0\), reduces to (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

4. Adds two \(v\max(\cdot)\) terms; can zero them, reduces to (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

5. Adds \(\max(\cdot)\) and \(v\max(\cdot)\) with \(|v|\); can zero extra terms, reduces to (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

6. Same story: zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

7. Has \(v\max(0,c5-|v|)\) piecewise; can set \(c4=0\) ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

8. Two Max terms; can set them 0 ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

9. Two \(v\max\) terms; can set them 0 ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

10. Max terms; can set them 0 ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

11. \(c0 v + c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\max(0,-v)+c4\cos t + c5\max(0,v)\). Piecewise linear in \(v\) unless \(c3=c5=0\). Then becomes (1)-like with \(\cos t\), still **no \(\sin(v)\)**. No.

12. Adds rational-in-\(t\) terms; can set those coefficients to 0, leaving \(c0 v + c1 e^{c2 t}+c7\cos t\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

13. Same as 12 plus constant; constants can be zeroed, still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

14. Includes \(v e^{c5 t}|v|\) and \(e^{c7 t}\cos(c8 t)\). Can zero nonlinear terms, and choose \(\cos(c8 t)\) to become \(\sin(t)\) only if \(c8=1\) and phase shift existed—but it’s \(\cos(c8 t)\) without phase parameter; still can match \(\sin(t)\) by using \(\cos(t)=\sin(t+\pi/2)\) only if phase shift allowed inside argument (it is not here). Even if we accept using \(\cos(t)\) as a shifted sine, **still no \(\sin(v)\)**. No.

15. Like 1 plus \(v e^{c5 t}|v|\); set \(c4=0\) ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

16. Has \(\max(0,c5+|v|)\) and \(v e^{c7 t}|v|\); can zero them ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

17. Rational-in-\(t\) plus constant; can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

18. \(c0 v + c1 e^{c2 t} + c6 + c7\cos t\) plus a \(t/(c4 t+c5)\) term. Zero nonmatching terms ⇒ linear+exp+cos+const; still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

19. Adds \(v e^{c5 t}|v|\) and \(v\max(\cdot)\); can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

20. Adds \(\max(\cdot)\) and \(v e^{c7 t}\); can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

21. Adds \(v\max(\cdot)\) and \(v e^{c7 t}\); can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

22. Adds complicated \(v e^{c7|v|}/(c8+|v|)\); can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

23. Adds \(e^{c7 t}|v|\); can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

24. Has two exponentials in \(t\), cos(t), and two \(v\max\) terms. You can set exp and max terms to 0, leaving \(c0 v + c5\cos t\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

25. Similar; can reduce to linear+cos, still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

26. Adds \(\log(c7 v^2+1)\cos(c8 t+c9)\). Even if you set \(c6=0\) to remove it, you’re back to (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). If not zero, it’s not \(\sin(v)\) anyway. No.

27. Adds \(v e^{c7 t}\cos t\) and Max term; can zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

28. Polynomial in \(v\) plus \(\cos t\) plus \(|v|^2\). To match GT you must kill \(v^3\) and \(|v|^2\) terms (set coefficients 0), leaving linear \(v\)+const+exp+cos. Still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

29. Adds \(e^{c5 t}|v|\); cannot become \(\sin(v)\). Zero it ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

30. Has \(\log(c5 v+1)\) and \(|v|^2\). Not \(\sin(v)\); can zero them, still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

31. Has \(e^{c4 v}\cos t\) and \(\sin(c7 t+c8)\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). Any \(v\)-dependence is exponential, not sinusoidal; can’t produce \(\sin(v)\) globally. No.

32. Has \(v\sin(c7 t+c8)|v|\) plus Max term; no \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

33. Has \(v(c6+t)^{c7}\) and \(|v|^2\). No \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ linear+exp+cos+const; still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

34. Adds \(v e^{c9 t}\) and rational-in-\(t\). No \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

35. Has \(e^{c4 v}\cos t\) and \(\sin(c6 t+c7)\). Still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

36. Has \(|v|^2\) and \(v e^{c7|v|}\). Not \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ linear+exp+cos+const; still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

37. Has Max terms and \(e^{c9 t}|v|\). No \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

38. Has \(v e^{c5 t}|v|\) and \(v e^{c7 t}\cos(c8 t)\). No \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

39. Has multiple \(v\max\) and \(v e^{c9 t}|v|\). No \(\sin(v)\). Zero extras ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

40. Similar; no \(\sin(v)\). No.

41. \(c0 + c1\sin(c2 t+c3) + c4 e^{c5 t + c6 v} + c7 v\). Can match \(\sin(t)\) by setting \(c2=1\) and phase \(c3=0\). But the only \(v\)-nonlinearity is \(e^{c6 v}\), not \(\sin(v)\). Setting \(c4=0\) removes it, leaving no \(\sin(v)\). No.

42. Has \(\cos(c7 e^{c8 t+c9 v})\) and \(|v|^2\). Not \(\sin(v)\). Can zero them, still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

43. Has \(\cos(c6 t)|v|^2\) and linear \(v\). No \(\sin(v)\). No.

44. Has \(e^{t}\log(\cdot |v|+1)\) type term. Not \(\sin(v)\). Zero it ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

45. Has logistic-like \(c6/(c7 e^{c8 t}+1)\). Not \(\sin(v)\). Zero it ⇒ (1) ⇒ no \(\sin(v)\). No.

46. Same as 45 but without \(v\max\) term; still no \(\sin(v)\). No.

47. \(c0 + c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\sin(c4 t+c5) + c6 e^{c7 v} + c8 e^{c9 v}\cos t\). No \(\sin(v)\); only exponentials in \(v\). No.

48. Linear \(v\) plus \(1/(t)\) terms plus \(\cos t\). No \(\sin(v)\). No.

49. Has \(v\max(\cdot)\) and \(\cos(c6 e^{c7 t+c8 v})\). Not \(\sin(v)\). No.

50. Has \(|v|^2\) and logistic-in-\(t\). No \(\sin(v)\). No.

Conclusion: every candidate lacks a term that can represent \(-0.484396978\sin(v)\) for all real \(v\). Since \(v\) can be negative and we need a true sinusoid in \(v\) (not piecewise, not absolute-value-based, not exponential/log), no parameter choice can make any candidate globally equal to the GT.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO3)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the GT: `-0.968793956035275*v + 0.106256914230442*sin(t) - 0.484396978017638*sin(v)`.

The GT has three basis functions: `v`, `sin(t)`, and `sin(v)`.

Key observations:
- `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t - π/2)`, so `cos(t)` with a phase shift could match `sin(t)` — but wait, the candidates use `cos(t)` not `cos(t + c)`. Since `cos(t)` and `sin(t)` are linearly independent, `c*cos(t)` alone cannot equal `sin(t)`. However, some candidates have additional terms involving `sin` with phase shifts.
- The GT requires a `sin(v)` term. This is a specific nonlinear function of `v` that cannot be replicated by polynomials, exponentials, `Abs(v)`, `Max` functions, `log`, or other non-sinusoidal functions of `v`.

Let me check each candidate for:
1. Can it produce `sin(t)` (or equivalent)?
2. Can it produce `sin(v)`?

**Critical issue:** Almost all candidates use `cos(t)` for the `t`-periodic term, not `sin(t)`. Since `cos(t)` and `sin(t)` are linearly independent, a single `cos(t)` term cannot match `sin(t)`. However, some candidates have additional oscillatory terms in `t` that could combine.

**Even more critical:** The GT requires `sin(v)`. Let me check which candidates have any sinusoidal function of `v`.

Scanning all candidates: None of the candidates contain `sin(v)` or `cos(v)` as a standalone term. The functions of `v` available are: `v`, `Abs(v)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `Max(0, ...)`, `exp(c*v)`, `log(c*v+1)`, `v**2`, `v**3`, polynomial/exponential combinations.

**None of these can produce `sin(v)`** because `sin(v)` is a transcendental oscillatory function that is linearly independent from all polynomials, exponentials, absolute values, max functions, and logarithms of `v`.

Let me double-check candidates with `exp(c*v)` terms (like 31, 35, 41, 47): Even combinations of exponentials in `v` produce `sinh(v)` or `cosh(v)`, not `sin(v)` (which would require imaginary exponents, but constants are real).

Candidate 31: `c0*v + c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*v)*cos(t) + c5*exp(c6*t)*sin(c7*t + c8)` — has `exp(c4*v)*cos(t)` which couples `v` and `t`, cannot produce `sin(v)` independently.

Candidate 35: `c0*v + c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*v)*cos(t) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7)` — `sin(c6*t+c7)` can match `sin(t)`, but no `sin(v)` term.

Candidate 47: `c0 + c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*exp(c7*v) + c8*exp(c9*v)*cos(t)` — has `exp(c7*v)` and `exp(c9*v)*cos(t)`, neither produces `sin(v)`.

**Conclusion:** Since `sin(v)` cannot be represented by any combination of the basis functions available in any candidate (polynomials, exponentials, absolute values, max functions, logarithms of `v`), **no candidate can match the GT**.
